Jamison Brereton

13 (204)
Indra
Gr╠еtsamada
13 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 13
The opening verses of this hymn leave the subject often unstated and often unclear in part because, as in the preceding hymns, there is often a double reference to ritual acts and either mythical or natural events. Thus, while details remain uncertain,

the first verses describe the soma sacrifice, seen as a creation of Indra. This ritual context is established in verse 1, in which the subject is likely the soma or the soma plant. The birth of the soma plant occurs in its proper time of year, and therefore its mother is the r╠еt├║, its тАЬseason.тАЭ However, the soma is also born at the proper ritual moment, and therefore its mother is also r╠еt├║, which can also refer to the тАЬritual sequence.тАЭ Then in verse 2, again without naming him, the poet introduces IndraтАФ or apparently does soтАФthrough associating IndraтАЩs release of the waters with the flowing, soma-bearing waters of the rite.
Verses 3тАУ4 describe the acts of the ritual, although in 4b, the identity of several of the actors is not certain. The one тАЬwho comesтАЭ could be soma or Indra or even the fire (as Geldner suggests with a different interpretation of the ellipsis). The poet turns to IndraтАЩs heroic deeds in verse 5тАФalthough the waters which he released connect these deeds to the ritualтАФand then in verse 6, to an explicit description of IndraтАЩs ritual acts. Verse 7 poses a number of interpretive difficulties, but in p─Бda a, the тАЬflowering and fruitfulтАЭ might be plants generally or the soma plants; in p─Бda b, the streams might be waters or specifically ritual waters; and in p─Бda d, the ┼лrv├б, the тАЬcontainers,тАЭ might refer to the oceans as containers of water in a cosmic register or the containers of soma in a ritual one.
Verses 8тАУ12 mention other of IndraтАЩs deeds. In verse 9 Geldner suggests that Indra bound his enemies by a magically induced sleep and thus by that тАЬwhich has no ropes.тАЭ See also II.15.9, where Indra conquers his enemies by putting them to sleep. Verse 12, returning to the conjunction of heroic and ritual deed and to the theme of rivers and waters, may speak not (or not only) of IndraтАЩs rescue of a per
son who was blind and lame, but of IndraтАЩs role in producing the soma hidden in the plant before it is pressed out (cf. II.15.7).

Jamison Brereton Notes

[II.13 Indra (misc. comments by SJ to JPB tr.) This hymn is extremely challenging, with a discouraging number of puzzles and no clear overall theme – though IndraтАЩs cosmogonic activities and his help to particular clients dominate the latter part of the hymn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe season (of the rains) is the parent (of the Soma), which, as soon as born of her, enters into the waters in which it grows; thence it is fit for expression, as concentrating (the essence of the) water, and the juice of the Soma is especially to be praised (as the libation proper for Indra).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

His mother is the season. From her, as soon as he was born, he [=soma] entered among the waters, in whom he grows strong.
Then he became a voluptuous woman, swelling with milk. The plantтАЩs first beestingsтАФthat one is worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (incl. JPB) seem to assume that p├бri serves as a postposition with t├бsy─Б(с╕е), but the interposition of ap├бс╕е and, esp., the close sandhi of ap├бs p├бri make this difficult. Jesse Lundquist suggests that ap├бс╕е might have a double reading, as a rare singular form of ├бp- тАШwaterтАЩ, an ablative to be read with t├бsy─Б(с╕е), and as the more usual acc. pl., with which the pl. rel. y─Б╠Бsu agrees. Thus тАЬjust born from this water he has entered the waters in which he grows strong.тАЭ But the most likely referent of t├бsy─Б(с╕е) is the immediately preceding j├бnitr─л, which refers to the season, so an abl. of water is unlikely. That p├бri might form a lexeme with ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыat is suggested by 8c ├бpariviс╣гс╣нam.

Note the alliteration in cd: pipy├║с╣г─л p├бyo тАж p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гam pratham├бm, with the first terms of each pair echoing each other. Jesse Lundquist suggests that ├бс╣Г┼Ы├│с╕е p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гam pratham├бm is in apposition to the p├бyaс╕е phrase, rather than being, with most tr. incl. JPBтАЩs, a nominative expressing the subject of ukthy├аm, anticipating t├бd. This would allow the refrain to be a separate clause, as it overwhelmingly is in the rest of the hymn.

Griffith

THE Season was the parent, and when born therefrom it entered rapidly the floods wherein it grows.
Thence was it full of sap, streaming with milky juice: the milk of the plant’s stalk is chief and meet for lauds.

Geldner

Die Jahreszeit ist seine Geb├дrerin. Von ihr geboren ging er alsbald ins Wasser, in dem er erstarkt. Da ward er eine ├╝ppige, von Milch strotzende Frau. Die erste Milch des Stengels, die ist preisenswert.

Grassmann

Die Zeit ward Mutter, und von ihr erzeugt ging rasch der Somazweig in Wasser ein, darin er schwillt; Da ward er saftig, eine Kuh, die strotzt von Milch; des Zweiges Biestmilch ist des h├╢chsten Preises werth.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe aggregated (streams) come, bearing everywhere the water, and conveying it as sustenance for the asylum of all rivers, (the ocean); the samepath is (assigned) to all the descending (currents) to follow; and as he, who has (assigned) them (their course), you, (Indra), are especially to be praised.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Toward a single goal they [=the waters] come, bringing milk throughout. They bring forth sustenance for him [=Indra?] who is all motherтАЩs milk (for us).
The downward sloping (watercourses) share the same road to flow along. You, who did these things first, are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pres. part. to the redupl. pres. b├нbhrat─лс╕е in a seems to contrast functionally with the finite injunc. (pr├б) bharanta in b, with the former expressing the regular, repetitive action of the waters bringing milk, while the latter expresses a one-time or at least notably separate action.

Griffith

They come trooping together bearing milk to him, and bring him sustenance who gives support to all.
The way is common for the downward streams to flow. Thou who didst these things first art worthy of our lauds.

Geldner

Sie laufen nach dem gemeinsamen Ziel, ihre Milch mit sich f├╝hrend, sie bringen ihm, der alle Formen annimmt, Nahrung: Die Str├╢me haben den gleichen Weg zu laufen. Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Dann dringen K├╝he, Milch ihm bringend, in ihn ein; der alles n├дhrt, dem bringen sie die Nahrung dar; Dieselbe Bahn zum Fliessen ist den st├╝rzenden; der dies du thatest, du bist h├╢chsten Preises werth.

Elizarenkova

рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛрдпрджреНрдзрд╡рд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛрджрджрд╛рддрд┐ рддрджреЗрдХреЛрд╣реЛрддрд╛рдиреБрд╡рджрддрд┐рдпрд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдкреБрд░реЛрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдГрд╕реНрдорд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ рдП- рдХреЛрдзреНрдпрд░реНрдпреБрдГ рд░реВрдкрд╛ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВрд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдорд┐рдирдиреН рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреН рддрджрдкрд╛рдГ рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╢рд╕рдирд╛рдЦреНрдпрдордкрдГрдХрд░реНрдордпрд╕реНрдпрддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрддреНрдИрдп- рддреЗ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдиреЗрд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдПрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреБрджрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рддрддреНрдХрд░реНрддреГрдХрд╛рдгрд┐рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкрдгрд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╡реИрдЧреБ- рдгреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐рддрд┐рддрд┐рдХреНрд╖рддреЗ рддрджреНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреНрддрдХрд░рдгреЗрдирдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╕рд╣рддреЗ рдЧреБрдкреНрддрд┐рдЬреНрдХрд┐рдбреНрднреНрдпрдГрд╕рдиреН рдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рдпрд╛рдорд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреЗ рддрд╛рдирд┐рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирд╛рджреАрдирд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдордХреГрдгреЛрд░рдХрд░реЛрдГ рд╕рддреНрд╡рдореБрдХреНрдереНрдпреЛрд╕рд┐ рее рей рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOne (priest) announces (the offering) that he, (the instrumental tutor of the rite) presents; another performs the act that apportions the limbs (of the victim); a third corrects all the deficiencies of either, and as he, who has enjoyed these (functions), your, (Indra), are especially to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hot─Б, Adhvaryu and Brahm─Б are the three priests indicated

Jamison Brereton

One [=the Hotar] accompanies what he gives with his speech. Another [=the Adhvaryu] hastens at his work, changing the forms (of
the soma).
He [=soma] withstands all the blows of another [=the pressing stone]. You, the one who did these things first, are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a is syntactically disturbing, in that it seems to have a clear embedded rel. cl.: ├бnv ├йko vadati y├бd d├бd─Бti t├бd, with t├бd the referent in the main cl.

corresponding to y├бd in the dependent cl. (тАЬ тАж that which he givesтАЭ – so the standard tr. incl. JPBтАЩs). Since such constructions seem strongly disallowed in RV, such a bald example would be striking and in fact begs for a different interpr. The interpr. of this p─Бda is made more difficult by the fact that the lexeme ├бnu тИЪvad is found only here in the RV and it is not entirely clear what action is being performed.

If S─Бyaс╣Зa/Geldner (et al.) are correct in identifying the first ├йkaс╕е as the Hotar and the second as the Adhvaryu, a possible solution emerges. The Hotar should not in fact be тАЬgivingтАЭ anything; his job is to recite in accompaniment (an activity well conveyed by ├бnu тИЪvad) to the ritual actions. It is the Adhvaryu who gives, that is, who actually makes the physical offering. Assuming that this division of labor already obtains in the RV, it seems likely to me that y├бd d├бd─Бti begins a new sentence and is a preposed rel. with the main cl. тАж ├йka ─лyate. I would tentatively tr. the hemistich тАЬOne follows along with this speech. the (other) one hastens when he gives that [=soma/oblation], changing its forms, having that as his work.тАЭ If y├бd is rather taken as the neut. rel.

pron., the tr. can be modified to тАЬWhat he gives, he hastens to that, having that as his work тАжтАЭ My working assumption is that the independent t├бd is coreferential with the t├бd in the cmpd t├бd-apas-.

Griffith

One priest announces what the institutor gives: one, altering the forms, zealously plies his task,
The third corrects the imperfections left by each. Thou who didst these things first art worthy of our lauds.

Geldner

Der eine begleitet mit Worten das, was er spendet; der eine, dessen Gesch├дft dies ist, geht hin und her, indem er dabei dessen Formen ver├дndert. Er h├дlt alle St├╢├Яe des einen aus. Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Was dar er reicht, begleitet einer mit dem Wort, ein andrer eilt gesch├дftig wechselnd die Gestalt, Des dritten St├╢sse alle h├дlt der Stengel aus; der dies du thatest, du bist h├╢chsten Preises werth.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬDistributing nourishment to their progeny, they, (the householders), abide (in their dwellings), as if offering ample and sustaining wealth to a guest; constructing (useful works, a man) eats with his teeth the food (given him) by (his) protector and as he, who has enjoined these (things to be done), you, (Indra), are especially to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Constructing useful works: asinvan daс╣Гс╣гс╣нraiс╕е pitur atti bhojanam: asinvan = setubandh─Бdikam karma kurvan, doing acts, such as building bridges and the like;

Pituс╕е = p─Бlaka, the fostering heaven, from which comes the rain that causes the growth of grain, for the sustenance of man

Jamison Brereton

They [=the priests] sit, apportioning prosperity to their children [=their fires], apportioning, like wealth, the back (of the fire?) as it arches
forth to him [=the soma?] who comes. Insatiable, he [=the fire] eats the food of his father [=the priest] with his teeth. You, the one who did these things first, are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Contra the standard tr. (incl. JPBтАЩs) I wonder if vibh├бjanta ─Бsate has тИЪ─Бs тАШsitтАЩ in auxiliary function as later: тАЬkeep XingтАЭ (in this case тАЬkeep distributingтАЭ) rather than having the literal sense тАЬthey sit, distributing.тАЭ I am baffled by p─Бda b.

Griffith

Dealing out food unto their people there they sit, like wealth to him who comes, more than the back can bear.
Greedily with his teeth he eats the master’s food. Thou who didst these things first art worthy of our lauds.

Geldner

Sie sitzen da, indem sie den Kindern den Vorrat austeilen. Dem Ankommenden begie├Яen sie den R├╝cken, der wie der Reichtum gr├╢├Яer wird. Ohne Bissen zu machen i├Яt er mit den Bei├Яz├дhnen die Speise seines Vaters. Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Den Ihren Nahrung spendend sitzt der Edlen Schar, wie Gut dem Gaste, das den R├╝cken ├╝berragt; Des Vaters Nahrung kaut mit Z├дhnen Agni keck; der dies du thatest, du bist h├╢chsten Preises werth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch as you have rendered earth visible to heaven, and have set open the path of the rivers by slaying Ahi; therefore the gods have rendered you divine by praises, as (men) invigorate a horse by water; (and) you are, (Indra), to be praised.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then you made the earth to see heavenтАФyou, who cleared the paths of the streams, o smasher of the serpent.
The gods gave birth to you, the god, by their praise songs, like a
winning horse by waters. You are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the causative infinitival phrase akс╣Ыс╣Зoс╕е pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Бс╣Г saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыe div├й, Renou and Witzel Got┼Н take dat. heaven as subj. and acc. earth as obj. of the dat. infinitive, in contrast to the published translation and Geldner Since the usual obj. of the infinitive dс╣Ы┼Ы├й is the sun, the Geldner/JPB interpr. seems more likely, in that it also involves looking heavenward. Note also that in 8ab the datives pс╣Ыkс╣г─Б╠Бya and d─Бs├бve┼Ы─Бya are objects of the dative infin. n├нhantave, with the same syntactic pattern as is suggested here. There is also an occurrence of the same stem saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы- in the acc. pl. in 10c, but this seems to have no clear relationship to the dative here and is, in any case, quite opaque.

Griffith

Thou hast created earth to look upon the sky: thou, slaying Ahi, settest free the river’s paths.
Thee, such, a God, the Gods have quickened with their lauds, even as a steed with waters: meet for praise art thou.

Geldner

Damals lie├Яest du die Erde den Himmel schauen, der du, o Drachent├╢ter, die Bahnen der Fl├╝sse freimachtest. Dich, den Gott, haben die G├╢tter mit Lobliedern wie ein Rennpferd mit Wasser neugeboren. Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Die Erde schufst du zu des Himmels Ebenbild, als, Ahit├╢dter, Quellen freie Bahn du schufst; Drum labten dich, gleich wie ein Ross durch Wassertrunk, durch Lob die G├╢tter dich den Gott, das ist dein Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(You are he) who bestows both food and increase, and milk the dry nutritious (grain) from out of the humid stalk; he, who gives wealth to the worshipper, and are sole sovereign of the universe you are he, (Indra), who is to be praised.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, who distribute sustenance and increase, have milked the dry [=the soma plant] together with its honey [=the soma] out of the wet
[=rain].
You have hidden a treasure [=soma] in Vivasvant [=the sun]. You alone are the master of everything. You are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Klein (DGRV I.135, etc.), I take the double ca as conjoining morphologically parallel bh├│janam and v├бrdhanam, despite the preposed position of the 2nd ca. This preposing would be supported by 7a where a correctly positioned second ca in a double ca construction is found in the same metrical position and before an almost rhyming final word, dh├бrmaс╣З─Б.

Because of the accent on dud├│hitha, p─Бda b must continue the relative cl. of p─Бda a, rather than serving as its main cl. as in the published translation, which should be corrected to тАЬYou, who distribute тАж and who have milked …, / you have hidden тАжтАЭ IтАЩm inclined to take the loc. viv├бsvati here as тАЬbei/chez VivasvantтАЭ rather than тАЬin VivasvantтАЭ as in the published translation That is, Indra set down a treasure in the vicinity of Vivasvant, presumably as a reward for VтАЩs sacrifice, rather than within his body.

Jesse Lundquist points out the complex mirror-image figure that straddles the p─Бda break in cd: #s├б тАж dadhiс╣гe viv├бsvati, v├н┼Ыvasya├нka ─л┼Ыiс╣гe s├б тАж The two interior elements, viv├бsvati and v├н┼Ыvasya├нka(с╕е), are phonologically similar and isosyllabic; they are flanked by 2nd sg. mid. perfects with rhyming ending -iс╣гe; and the pronoun s├б with 2nd sg. reference provides an outer ring.

Griffith

Thou givest increase, thou dealest to us our food: thou milkest from the moist the dry, the rich in sweets.
Thou by the worshipper layest thy precious store: thou art sole Lord of all. Meet for our praise art thou.

Geldner

Der du die Nahrung und Gedeihen austeilst, aus dem Feuchten das Trockene und S├╝├Яe gemolken hast, du hast dir bei Vivasvat einen Schatz angelegt. Du allein gebeust ├╝ber alles - Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Der Nahrung du vertheilest und Gedeihen schaffst, und aus dem Feuchten zogst die trockne, s├╝sse Frucht, Bei dem Vivasvat legtest du den Schatz dir hin; allein besitzest alles du; das ist dein Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдкрд┐рдгреАрдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдкрд╡рддреАрд╢реНрдЪрдкреНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕реВрддрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕реВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╡рдиреАрд░рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реАрд░реЛрд╖рдзреАрдГ рджрд╛рдиреЗрдзрд┐ рджреАрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдЙрдкрд▓реВрдпрдиреНрддреЗрд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпрддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐рджрд╛рдирдЩреНрдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░рдВ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдгреЗрд▓реНрдпреБрдЯреН рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдХреНрд╖реЗрддреНрд░реЗ рдзрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рд╕рдХрд▓рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрдирдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдЪ рд╡реНрдпрдзрд╛рд░рдпрдГ рдиреНрдпрджрдзрд╛рдГ рдпрд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рдиреНрджрд┐рд╡реЛрджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрдЕрд╕рдорд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╛рдГ рдирд╛рдирд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджрд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдГ рджреАрдкреНрддреАрдГ рд░рдЬрдирдГ рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЬрдиреЗрд░реНрд▓рдЩрд┐рд╡реНрдпреНрддрддреНрдпрдпреЗрдирд╢рдкреН рдпрд╢реНрдЪреЛрд░реБрдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдКрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдорд╣рддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд┐рдХрд╛рдпрд╛рдиреН рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдардВрд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрдореН рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou who have caused, by culture, the flowering and fruitful (plural nts) to spread over the field; who have genitive rated the various luminaries of heaven; and who, of vast bulk, comprehend vast (bodies); you are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, who established separately the flowering and fruitful (plants) according to the foundation (of each) and the streams at their
division;
and you, who gave birth to the unequalled flashings of heaven; you, the wide one surrounding the containersтАФyou are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

d─Б╠Бna- in b is almost universally taken as тАШpastureтАЩ (Weide) or тАШearthтАЩ (Renou тАШsur terreтАЩ), a meaning attributed to d─Б╠Бna- only in this passage. The interpr. goes back, one way or the other, to S─Бyaс╣Зa: upal┼лyante sasy─Бny atreti d─Бnaс╣Г kс╣гetram. His remark тАЬgrain is cut thereтАЭ implies a connection with тИЪd─Б тАШreap, mowтАЩ (EWAтАЩs D─А2 ). His gloss тАШfieldтАЩ (d─Бnaс╣Г kс╣гetram) is repeated thereafter, most influentially in BR, though they seem to derive the word from тИЪd─Б тАШdivideтАЩ (EWAтАЩs D─А4 ); subsequent adoptors of the gloss do not bother to comment on the etymology. S─Бyaс╣ЗaтАЩs implied derivation from тИЪd─Б тАШreapтАЩ is appealing. There are several clear exx. of the root pres. of this root in the RV (grouped under GrassmannтАЩs 2. d─Б), as well as nominal derivatives (see EWA s.v. D─А2 ). The reference in this vs. to the establishment of flowering and fruitful plants would have helped preserve a lexical item specific to agriculture, even though it is homonymous with the more common d─Б╠Бna- тАШgiftтАЩ (and see differently accented d─Бn─Б╠Бya тАШto give, for givingтАЩ in 13a).

I wonder, however, about the concrete locational sense that S─Бyaс╣Зa gives it; it might make more sense as an abstract тАШin their reapingтАЩ. The vs. seems to depict Indra as the orderer of the cosmos, with the solemn etymological figure dh├бrmaс╣З─Б тАж ├бdh─Бrayaс╕е тАЬyou established by your establishmentтАЭ (or without English cognate expression, тАЬyou established by your ordinanceтАЭ). (I would not follow JPBтАЩs attribution of the dh├бrman- to the plants: тАЬaccording to the foundation (of each).тАЭ) Most of the hemistich would then show Indra creating the various plants in their crucial function, to be harvested. (The presence of ├бdhi might be counter-evidence to my interpr., in that it generally has a locational sense, but IтАЩm not certain that this is enough to derail it.) I further think that the last bit of the hemistich, vy ├аv├бn─лr ├бdh─Бrayaс╕е, is a somewhat separate expression. That is, I read ├бdh─Бrayaс╕е without preverb with the тАЬplantsтАЭ segment in p─Бda a / first part of b (thus not flg. JPBтАЩs тАЬestablished separately the flowering and fruitful (plants)тАЭ), and restrict v├н тАж ├бdh─Бrayaс╕е to the streams of the end of b; its position after the caesura in b favors this syntactic separation. If this interpr. is correct, the problematic d─Б╠Бne may require further analysis, for in addition to тАШin their reapingтАЩ for the first part of the hemistich (to тИЪd─Б тАШreapтАЩ) it could also be taken as a derivative of тИЪd─Б тАШdivideтАЩ, as JPB does: тАШin their divisionтАЩ. It is ideally positioned to be read with both.

I would thus tr. the hemistich тАЬYou who established by your ordinance the flowering and fruitful (plants) in their reaping (and) established the (various) streams separately in their division.тАЭ IndraтАЩs division of undifferentiated water into separate streams would be part of his fructifying project – bringing life-giving water to the various terrestrial regions.

Having created the relevant features of the earth – plants and streams – in ab, Indra then turns to a particular heavenly feature, the didy├║t-s. What exactly is meant here isnтАЩt clear. The stem didy├║t-, like its near-twin didy├║-, generally means тАШmissile, dartтАЩ, but often a missile sent flying from heaven by a god (cf., e.g., VII.46.3 [Rudra] y─Б╠Бte didy├║d ├бvasс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─Б div├бs p├бri тАЬwhich missile of yours shot downward from heaven тАжтАЭ). As Mayrhofer points out (EWA s.v. didy├║-), didy├║t- has probably been remodeled after тИЪdyot or vidy├║t- тАШlightningтАЩ (IтАЩd favor the latter). And often it seems to have a naturalistic aspect, as lightning (or the dreaded тАШthunderboltтАЩ of oldfashioned Vedic exegesis). Here the naturalistic reading seems esp. prominent, and I suggest that ├бsama- тАШunequalledтАЩ may also have the sense тАШunequalтАЩ – that is, jagged and asymmetrical, zigzaging like lightning.

The last difficulty of this challenging verse is the first part of d, ur├║r ┼лrv─Б╠Бm╠Р abh├нtaс╕е. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) and the published translation take this as an independent nominal clause (e.g., JPB: тАЬyou, the wide one surrounding the containersтАЭ). Given the cosmogonic cast of the rest of the vs., I would follow Renou, who takes ┼лrv─Б╠Бn as a 2nd object of ├бjanaс╕е in c: тАЬ(qui,) vaste (toi-m├кme, as engendr├й) les mers tout autours.тАЭ Although ┼лrv├б-, lit.

тАШcontainerтАЩ, generally refers to cow-pens and the like in the RV, RenouтАЩs тАШseasтАЩ (as particularly large containers) seems correct here; cf. the same usage, also in Maс╣Зс╕Нala II, in II.35.3, where the rivers all fill тАЬthe same ┼лrv├б-тАЭ (sam─Бn├бm ┼лrv├бс╣Г nady├ас╕е pс╣Ыс╣Зanti). I would thus tr. cd тАЬand who begot the unequal(led) flashing missiles of heaven (and) the тАШcontainersтАЩ [=seas] all about, (you) the wide one.тАЭ The juxtaposition ur├║r ┼лrv─Б╠Бn is a play on words; the two are not etymologically related, at least by most lights.

What is striking about this vs. is that, unlike the usual cosmogonic vss., which refer to large generic parts of creation (heaven, earth, etc.), this one highlights particular idiosyncratic aspects of the grand cosmic divisions.

Griffith

Thou who hast spread abroad the streams by stablished law, and in the field the plants that blossom and bear seed;
Thou who hast made the matchless lightnings of the sky,-vast, compassing vast realms, meet for our praise art thou.

Geldner

Der du die bl├╝henden und fruchttragenden Pflanzen nach der Ordnung und die Fl├╝sse ├╝ber das Feld verteilt hast, und der du die unvergleichlichen Geschosse des Himmels erzeugtest, selbst breit die Meere ringsum ausgebreitet hast. - Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Der auf der Trift du, was erbl├╝ht und Samen tr├дgt, und B├дche auch vertheiltest, wie’s die Ordnung heischt, Und der des Himmels pr├дcht’ge Blitze du erschufst und Wolkenbecken weit darum, das ist dein Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, who are (famed for) many exploits, put on today an unclouded countenance, (as prepared) to slay Sahavasu, the son of Nс╣Ыmara, with the sharpened (edge of the thunderbolt), in defence of the (sacrificial) food, and for the destruction of dasyu; you are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sahavasu, the son of Nс╣Ыmara: two asuras; nс╣Ыman and mara = who kills;

Saha = with;

Vasu = wealth

Jamison Brereton

You, who, in order to strike down Pr╠еkс╣гa and D─Бsave┼Ыa, conveyed the son of Nr╠еmara together with his goods
to the impregnable mouth of the ┼кrjayant─л (River) and who even today (would do likewise); you, who do many deedsтАФyou are worthy
of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

To avoid the need to supply additional unsupported material (JPBтАЩs тАЬwould do likewiseтАЭ) to the brief beginning of p─Бda d uta├нv─Б╠Бdy├б purukс╣Ыt, I interpr. purukс╣Ыt as a predicated voc. (тАЬand even today (you are) a much-doerтАЭ), with most tr.

Griffith

Who broughtest Narmara with all his wealth, for sake of food, to slay him that the fiends might be destroyed,
Broughtest the face unclouded of the strengthening one, performing much even now, worthy art thou of praise.

Geldner

Der du den Narmara samt seinen Sch├дtzen , um den Priksa und Dasavesa zu erschlagen, nach dem unbesetzten Eingang von Urjayanti fuhrest, auch heute noch tatenreich bist du darum preisenswert.

Grassmann

Der du f├╝r Prikscha und f├╝r Dasaveca auch, zu tilgen auszogst Narmara mit seinem Gut, Der starken Sonne unverh├╝lltes Antlitz fuhrst, auch heute noch vielwirkender, das ist dein Ruhm.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, for whose sole plural asure a thousand (steeds are ready); by whom all are to be fed; and who protects the instrumental tutor (of the sacrifice); who, for the sake of Dabh─лti, has caste the Dasyus into unfettered (captivity), and who are to be approached (by all), you are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dabh─лti: a с╣Ыс╣гi; he is elsewhere called a r─Бj─Б; several exploits here attributed to Indra are attributed to A┼Ыvins

Jamison Brereton

Or when you helped him, the hard-driving oneтАФat whose obedience (to you), though he was alone, you bound his hundred times ten
(enemies) all at onceтАФ
you tied up the Dasyus for Dabh─лti in what has no ropes, and you
belonged to him who ritually pursues you well. You are worthy
of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntax of the 1st hemistich is intricate and hard to parse. The first rel. cl.

(тАж y├бsya тАж) extends through ├йkasya ┼Ыruс╣гс╣нa├║, with y├бsya coreferential with ├йkasya.

This clause is in turn dependent on the short y├бd clause y├бd dha cod├бm ─Б╠Бvitha, with cod├бm the referent of y├бsya. The standard tr. take cod├б- as a personal name, but this is not necessary, as Mayrhofer (PN s.v.) points out – and in fact it would be better not to have another name for Dabh─лti (c), who is the ultimate referent of both y├бsya (a) and cod├бm (b).

Note that ─Б╠Бdiya(с╕е) at the end of b matches ─Бs├нyam at end of 8c.

Griffith

Thou boundest up the Dasa’s hundred friends and ten, when, at one’s hearing, thou belpest thy worshipper.
Thou for Dabhiti boundest Dasyus not with cords; Thou wast a mighty help. Worthy of lauds art thou.

Du wardst der Helfer des gut Zuredenden - Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou are he, from whose manhood all the rivers (have proceeded); to whom (the pious) have given (offerings); to whom, doer of mighty deeds, they have presented wealth; you are he, who have regulated the six expansive (objects), and are the protector of the five (races), that look up to you; you are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Six expansive objects: с╣гad. vistiraс╕е = heaven, earth, day, night, water and plural nts

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour heroism, hero, is to be glorified, by which, with single effort, you have acquired wealth; (wherewith) the (sacrificial) food of (every) solemn and constant (ceremony is provided); for all (the acts) you have performed, you, Indra, are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wherewith the sacrificial food: j─Бt┼лс╣гс╣нhirasya pra vayaс╕е sahasvato: j─Бtuс╣гс╣нhara may be a proper name; i.e. you have given (pra = pradaс╕е) food to the vigorous j─Бtuс╣гс╣нhara; alternatively, Indra being the occasional (j─Бtu) agent in sacrificial offerings (vayas) in relation to constant and essential ceremonies: sthirasya balavato yaj├▒─Бdeс╕е karmaс╣Зaс╕е sambandhi vayas

Jamison Brereton

Your heroism, o hero, is good to proclaim: that by your resolve alone you take possession of goods.
The vigor (belonging to you, who are) born steadfast and possessing strength, is preeminent. All the things that you have doneтАФ(for
these) you, Indra, are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda, suprav─Бcan├бс╣Г t├бva v─лra v─лry├аm, is a nominalization of the famous opening of I.32 (found in various forms elsewhere): ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├б vocam. In that hymn this opening is followed by the account of an undoubted heroic deed, the slaying of Vс╣Ыtra. Here the specification in b, introduced by y├бd (as often in such proclamations) followed by a promisingly heroic ├йkena kr├бtun─Б тАЬby your resolve alone,тАЭ turns out to be something of an anticlimax: you find goods. This lack of drama is somewhat repaired by d, which sketches a larger world of great deeds.

Unfortunately, however, the syntax of d is disturbing. The rel. cl. of d is universally tr. (incl. by JPB) тАЬall the things you have done,тАЭ but тАЬallтАЭ (v├н┼Ыv─Б) is not part of the rel. cl. (y─Б╠Бcak├бrtha). It has instead been stuck in the refrain, which only in this verse has been altered from s─Б╠Бsi ukthy├ас╕е (2-10d, 12d) to s├йndra v├н┼Ыv─Бsi ukthy├ас╕е.

Dropping a piece of a rel. cl. into the middle of a main cl. is simply impossible in the RV. It is possible to interpr. v├н┼Ыv─Б as a real part of the main cl., an acc. of respect: тАЬWhat (deeds) you have done, you are worthy of hymns with regard to all of them.тАЭ But somehow I doubt thatтАЩs what the poet intended – though what his intentions were, esp. given the deliberate alteration of the refrain, are opaque to me.

Another possible wrinkle in d is that y─Б╠Бneed not be the neut. pl. of the rel., illegally anticipating the v├н┼Ыv─Б intruding in the refrain. It could be an instr. sg. picking up v├бyaс╕е in the preceding p─Бda: тАЬтАж the vigor by which you have done тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Meet for high praise, O Hero, is thy power, that with thy single wisdom thou obtainest wealth,
The life-support of conquering Jatusthira. Indra, for all thy deeds, worthy of lauds art thou.

Geldner

Sch├╢nen Preis verdient deine Heldenkraft, du Held, da du mit einem einzigen Entschlu├Я das Gut verlangst. Die Kraft des Sieghaften, der von Natur standfest ist, tat sich hervor. Was du alles getan hast - Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Grassmann

Sehr hoch zu preisen, Held, ist deine Heldenthat, dass du das Gut auf einen Anlauf dir gewannst, Den Unterhalt des m├дchtigen Dschatuschthira; dass, Indra, du dies alles thatest, ist dein Ruhm.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have provided a passage for the easy crossing of the flowing waters for Turvati and Vayya; rendering (yourself) renowned, you have uplifted the blind and lame Paravс╣Ыj from the lowliness (of affliction); you are he who is to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You have provided a passage: aramaya sarapasastar─Бya srutim: apas = karma; saraс╣Зam apaс╕е karma y─Бsaс╕е, they of whom the act is going or proceeding; the person ns named beheld a large river, which they were unable to cross, when the prayed to Indra, and were conveyed across by him; the blind and lame Par─Бvс╣Ыj: par─Бvс╣Ыjam pr─Бndham ┼Ыroс╣Зam: added, cakс╣гase etave, to see and to walk; the name of с╣Ъjra┼Ыva is understood, as the individual who was made to see; Sroс╣Зa was the name of him who was made to walk; pr─Бndha (blind) and ┼Ыrona (lame) were epithets of Par─Бvс╣Ыj

Jamison Brereton

You halted the course of the Sarapas (River) for Turv─лti and Vayya to cross.
You led him up who was sunk down and shunned, making famed the blind one and the lame. You are worthy of hymns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The use of the secondarily shortened stem ┼Ыrav├бya- here instead of inherited ┼Ыr─Бv├бya- may have been favored by the similarly short-root-vowel ├бramayaс╕е at the beginning of this vs. (which stem comes by its short root vowel honestly) and by the denom. ┼Ыravasy├б- in the next vs. More problematic is what pr├б тАж ┼Ыrav├бyan is conveying here. One might think that what the blind and the lame want is not fame but healing. Some such consideration must have led Grassmann to assign this form (and pr─Б╠Б┼Ыr─Бvayam X.49.8) to a different root ┼Ыru and a different idiom pr├б тИЪ┼Ыru тАШvorw├дrts bringenтАЩ. I see no justification for such a separation. It is possible that the causative here means (as it can elsewhere) тАШmake hear/heedтАЩ rather than тАШmake heard/famedтАЩ, though this wouldnтАЩt appreciably improve the situation of the blind and lame. Or that in the idiom pr├б тИЪ┼Ыru, the pr├б came to dominate, with a sense тАШfurther, favor (through fame)тАЩ.

Griffith

Thou for Turviti heldest still the flowing floods, the river-stream for Vayya easily to pass
Didst raise the outcast from the depths, and gavest fame unto the halt and blind. Worthy of lauds art thou.

Du hie├Яest die zu flie├Яen gewohnten Fl├╝sse stillstehen zum Durchschreiten, f├╝r Turviti und Vayya machtest du einen Weg. Den Aussetzling, der in der Tiefe steckte, holtest du herauf, der du dem Blinden, dem Lahmen zu Ruf verhalfst - Der du dies zuerst gemacht hast, - darum bist du preisenswert.

Du s├дnftigest dem Vajia zum Uebergang des schnellen Wassers Str├╢mung dem Turviti auch, Du halfst dem Kr├╝ppel, der tief unten lag, heraus den Blinden, Lahmen leitend, das auch ist dein Ruhm.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPossessor of riches, exert your ability to bestow wealth upon us; for yours is great affluence; may you, Indra, be disposed to grant us exceeding abundance day by day, so that, blessed with worthy descendants, we may glorify you at (our) sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Make your aim to give that gift to us, o good oneтАФyour store of goods is greatтАФ

the bright (gift), o Indra, through which you will seek fame throughout the days. тАУ May we speak loftily at the ritual distribution, in
possession of good heroes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The last puzzle in the hymn is found in p─Бda c and also involves fame. We have just urged Indra to to give us a r─Б╠Бdhaс╕е (тАШgift, benefitтАЩ) in the first hemistich. In c we find the phrase y├бc citr├бс╣Г ┼Ыravasy─Б╠Б(с╕е). Since citr├б- very frequently modifies r─Б╠Бdhaс╕е, it seems natural to supply the recently mentioned r─Б╠Бdhaс╕е here. But then what is Indra doing? y├бc citr├бm appears to be the obj. of ┼Ыravasy─Б╠Б(с╕е). But this denom. doesnтАЩt otherwise take an object (IV.42.2 cited by Grassmann is to be otherwise interpr.), and even if it did, the phrase would have to mean тАЬwhich bright (gift) you will seek as fame,тАЭ which doesnтАЩt seem to make sense. Geldner essentially tr. it this way (тАЬтАж eine ansehnliche (Lohngabe) тАж in der du тАж deinen Ruhm suchenтАЭ), but I donтАЩt see why Indra would be looking for his fame in that direction. JPB avoids the syntactic difficulty by tr. as if y├бc citr├бm were an instr.: тАЬthe bright gift through which you will seek fameтАЭ (my italics), but this still requires the gift to be something that would provide Indra with fame. RenouтАЩs tendency to supply masses of material to smoothe over the rough places is on full display here: тАЬce qui est ├йclatant, veuille le donner-pard├йsir de-renomтАЭ (so hyphenated). Witzel Got┼Н seem to have arrived at a novel solution, apparently separating citr├бm from its usual formulaic partner r─Б╠Бdhas and supplying ┼Ыr├бvas- тАШfameтАЩ – or so I interpret тАЬdamit du тАж deinen ansehnlichen Ruhm suchen m├╢gest.тАЭ However, as far as I can tell, ┼Ыr├бvas- is never modified by citr├б-, and context favors r─Б╠Бdhas- as referent. I have no solution. The least unsatisfactory may be to assume that, in our self-serving way, we are telling Indra that giving us a good gift will bring him fame (better than heroic deeds? see 11ab) – and in some sense it will, since we celebrate his generosity with hymns providing lasting ┼Ыr├бvas-.

Griffith

Prepare thyself to grant us that great bounty, O Vasu, for abundant is thy treasure.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН) (рддрддреН) (рд╡рд╕реЛ) рд╕реБрдЦреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддрд╛ (рджрд╛рдирд╛рдп) (рд░рд╛рдзрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗрди рддрддреН (рд╕рдорд░реНрдердпрд╕реНрд╡) рд╕рдорд░реНрдердВ рдХреБрд░реБ (рдмрд╣реБ) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╡рд╕рд╡реНрдпрдореН) рд╡рд╕реБрд╖реБ) рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рднрд╡рдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдж (рдпрддреН) (рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рдореН) рдЕрджреНрднреБрддрдореН (рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрд╕реБ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╡рдГ (рдЕрдиреБ) (рджреНрдпреВрдиреН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдиреН (рдмреГрд╣рддреН) рдорд╣рддреН (рд╡рджреЗрдо) (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╢реМрд░реНрдпреЛрдкреЗрддреИрд░реНрдЬрдиреИрд░реНрдЧреБрдгреИрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ реерезрейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдд рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рдпреЗрд╜рдиреНрдпрдЮреНрдЫрд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордмрд▓рдпреЛрдЧреЗрди рд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдЮреНрдЫреВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдирдГ рд╕рдВрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ реерезрейрее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдЗрддрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╢рд░реАрд░, рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рд╡ рдмрд▓рд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдпреЛрдЧрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рдорд░реНрде, рдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдп, рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░ рд╡ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереА рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреЗрдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рее резрей рее
